      "content after edit": [
        "Lastly, this case has a structure almost identical to the many-to-many on the left. Whereas the many-to-many structure seen in the previous slide reads the entire input sequence data up to the last time step before predicting the output sequence one step at a time,\n\nThis case can be viewed as a many-to-many task that does not allow any delay, predicting the output immediately from the 1st time step while reading the input sequence. For example, when a sequence of images is given in each frame of a video, rather than watching the entire video and then predicting an output sequence, it requires producing the necessary prediction values in real-time for each input frame without any latency. An example of this would be an object tracking task where the location of a specific object must be predicted immediately in each frame."

        "Lastly, this case has a structure almost identical to the many-to-many on the left. Whereas the many-to-many structure seen in the previous slide reads the entire input sequence data up to the last time step before predicting the output sequence one step at a time,\n\nThis case can be viewed as a many-to-many task that does not allow any delay, predicting the output immediately from the 1st time step while reading the input sequence. For example, when a sequence of images is given in each frame of a video, rather than watching the entire video and then predicting an output sequence, it requires producing the necessary prediction values in real-time for each input frame without any latency. An example of this would be an object tracking task where the location of a specific object must be predicted immediately in each frame."
